‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É approving of his daughter who had been seduced (with whom you had carnal intercourse).
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•=‡§∂‡§ï‡•Å‡§Ç‡§§‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ç. ‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ are, like a thief, regarded as a worthy recipient (of the gift). ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Ç a convincing reply.

VII.

‡§â‡§™‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§Ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§â‡§¶‡§ï‡•á‡§® was enticed (near you) by means of water i. e. was coaxed to drink water. ‡§∏‡§ó‡§Ç‡§ß akin or related.
‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç accomplishing or serving their own purpose.
‡§Ö‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§™‡§ü‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç untaught cunning or cleverness.

‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§® …….‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§É let those, who have studied how to deceive others, as if it were an art, be considered as trustworthy.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§Éhell, perdition.
‡§â‡§™‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ is admitted to be.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§§‡•Å but if ‡§™‡§∞‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π the wife of another.
‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‚Äî‡§§‡§¶‡§æ since-because, so-therefore.

VIII.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Ä‡§§‡§É large, extensive.

IX.

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡•ã‡§™‡§ó‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø (‡§®‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø) to him who approaches him for the first time.

‡§ï‡§∞‡§§‡§≤‡§æ…….. ‡§Ü‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç looking at the whole universe as if it were placed on the palm of their hands.

‡§∏‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç a sacrifice.

‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§¨‡§Ç‡§ß‡•á‡§® unimpeded, unobstructed.

‡§∂‡§Æ‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ etc.‚Äî‡§∂‡§Æ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§¨‡•á‡§≤‡§æ (‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ) ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≤‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç‡§ó‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®; the destructive wave to the boundary in the form of selfrestraint.
‡§â‡§™‡§®‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç having bowed down to him, seeking his protection.

‡§Æ‡§¶‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç censure consequent on pride or intoxication.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§•‡§æ‡§É the fates or destinations (births in other lives) have different ways according to their actions (in this world).

‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‚Äì‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•á ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•á ‡§à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§ placed.

XX.

‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•É‡§™‡§É as to how a king should act.

ficatory rite(‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞) initiating (one) to the study of the Vedas, i. e. being invested with the sacred thread.
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø having drawn out portions or essences (‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø).
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç who unguardedly or carelessly draws near.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•á shows himself in various aspects (‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§É ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§â‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø).
‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É the goddess of wealth, wealth (in general).
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç rule, course of conduct. ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§∑‡•Å in regard to desired objects. ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç might lay down.
‡§Ö‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç a prohibitive rule.
‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç should not break or transgress.
‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ú‡§Ç a son in the form of Dharma (duty) itself.
‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á become fit to enjoy (their respective rights etc.).
‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§É : as may be deserved, as is fit.
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç should inflict.
‡§∏ ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§¶‡§Ç‡§°‡§É‚Äî construe ‡§∏ ‡§¶‡§Ç‡§° ‡§è‡§µ (‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡•ã) ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É etc.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç the order of things would be topsy-turvy (upside down) what is at the bottom would rise to the top.
‡§¶‡§Ç‡§°‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§É held in check (controlled) by punishment.
‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡•Ä‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É controlled, restrained.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç by the non-infliction of.
‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§æ inflictor of the punishment.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡§É not evenhanded, or passionate.
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É is difficult to be (properly) used by those whose minds are not well trained (in duty).

‡§ò‡§®‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡§æ‡§π………‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ï‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§É by means of particular surgical instruments called, ‡§ï‡§Ç‡§ï‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ the points of which cannot be blunted by thick mail‚Äîcoats.

‡§≤‡•Ç‡§®‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§ï‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ç‡§°‡§É with his bow, the string of which was cut down.

‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§Æ‡§ø shall cause his memory alone to be left behind i. e. shall kill him.
‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§æ‡§§‡§ò‡•ã‡§∑ & c. the sound of whose bowstring was terrible like that of a thunder-stroke (or contending vapours).

XXIII.

‡§®‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§ò‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É scorched by heat.

‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§´‡§£‡§æ & c, whose body was irradiated by the resplendent (lit, casting rays upwards) gems on his several hoods,
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§ñ‡§≤‡•á whose zone (worn round the loins) was hidden under her silken garment (so as not to hurt his soft feet),
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§°‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç & c. (1) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§°‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï ‡§á‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø (2) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§™‡•Å‡§Ç‡§°‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø.
‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡§Ç (1) ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡§™‡§®‡§ø‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø (2) ‡§¨‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡§™‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§Ç (‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç) ‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç (1) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§É ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø‡§®‡§É ( ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§É ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ) ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç, (2) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç.
‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§£‡§Ç serving as a mirror to Lakshmi to see her graces in.
‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§ß antipathy to Shesha (the lord of serpents).
‡§∏‡•å‡§ñ‡§∂‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§ï one who asks another person whether he has slept well or has had comfortable sleep.
‡§Ö‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§ó‡•ã‡§ö‡§∞‡§Ç beyond the range of words and mind (i e. indescribable and inconceivable).
‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡§æ in three different capacities, viz. that of the creator,

that of the protector and that of the destroyer of the universe.
‡§è‡§ï‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç of one taste (sweet).
‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç & c. so you assume different states in the different qualities (i. √®. you become the creator in the satvaguna, protector in the rajoguna and destroyer in the tamoguna).
‡§Ö‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•Ä free from desire. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§É fulfiller of requests or desires.
‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç being indeterminate (extrmely subtle ), you are the cause of the determinate or developed ( world ).
‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§´‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç knowledge leading to the acquisition of the four, viz. ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ, ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•, ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ & ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑. ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É periods of time.
‡§™‡§Ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§µ‡§É the means of accomplishing the ends of human existence.
‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á not to return (to worldly life) again, i. e.to obtain final beatitude.
‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø indescribable and inconceivable, inscrutable.
‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® & c . that our words, having extolled. your greatness, are curtailed (fall short), is either through our exhaustion or inability (to describe) and not because your merits are limited.

‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§¶‡§Ç range with words faltering through fear or fright.

XXV.

‡§â‡§™‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç full of reasoning, argumentative.
‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§Ç spirited or noble.
‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø having seen all round, i. e. after careful consideration or circumspection. ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø may go with or ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Ç.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ã‡§™‡§ø & c. the meaning is that it is very easy to enter the deepest water by means of the stairs of a landing-place, but it is very difficult to find out the person who would make them; so it is very easy to comprehend the most difficult principles of polity (statesmanship) when duly enunciated, but the person who would enunciate them is rare to find.
‡§Ö‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø ‡§≠‡•á‡§∑‡§ú‡•á ‡§á‡§µ as in a medicine, small in quantity but very powerful in quality or efficacy.

‡§¨‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç given handed over. ‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§≤‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á,

‡§∂‡•ã‡§£ red ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§£‡§® plighting, promising.

XXVII.

‡§∑‡§°‡•ç‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§É the six remedies to be adopted by a king in his foreign relations are:‚Äî

‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ß‡§ø peace, ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π war, ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§® marching against, ‡§Ü‡§∏‡§® halt ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø taking shelter and ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§ß‡•Ä‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ duplicity.
‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§É the three parts of royal or regal power being (1) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Å‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø the majesty of the king, (2) ‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø the power of good counsel, and (3) ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§π‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§øthe power of energy.
‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É the three states, called ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø, ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø & ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®.
‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø having studied works, i. e. mere book-worms. ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§≤‡§Ç are competent to state or explain.
‡§Ö‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø & c. the array of words (mere bombast) of a talkative person, who has not well considered the work to be done (who has had no practical experience of any work), is useless.
‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï an archer, ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á‡§∑‡•Å‡§É ad unskilful archer ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç a target. ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ß ‡§á‡§µ like a timid warrior.
‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç = ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≤‡§Ç‡§¨‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç cannot brook delay.
‡§â‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•É to accept. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is displayde, spread.
‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§£ = ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•á‡§® highest.
‡§∏‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø considers himself well off or comfortable.
‡§®‡•á‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø at do not rise or become victorious.
‡§Ö‡§ñ‡§ø‡§≤‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø without having completely put down.
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§É goes with ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç.
‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§ó‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç & c. an artificial friend and an artificial foe are preferable; for they become so by the force of circumstances (i. e. by favours shown or injuries done), whereas natural and ordinary friends and foes may become enemies or friends ( as may suit their particular purpose).
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§É scil. ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç should be regarded as the characteristic or distinguishing marks( of the two).
‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§É offended.
‡§Ü‡§≤‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç do not say. ‡§¨‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§É name of a Yadava.
‡§®‡§∞‡§É nom. pl. (of ‡§®‡•É). ‡§ï‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á in dry grass or wood, or in the arm-pit.
‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡•ç may he not live, cursed be he who &c.
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å & c……‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§É may he not be born, may he cease to exist.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã‡§π‡§§‡§ø mounts the head (of the very person who tramples it under foot).
‡§Ö‡§™‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç is better than a person who, though insulted, remains quiet.
‡§§‡•Å‡§Ç‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•å & c. in the mountain there is elevation or height, but not the other, i. e. great depth or unfathomableness (‡§Ö‡§ó‡§æ‡§ß‡§§‡§æ) ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§£ soil. ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§§‡•á.
‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Å‡§ü‡§Ç evidently.
‡§Ö‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•å ‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø when the most insignificant enemy arrives, or when the slightest breeze begins to blow,. (‡§™‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ ‡§™‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç).
‡§¶‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§ø though at a great distance,
‡§™‡§Ç‡§ö‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç an ascetic who in summer practises penance sitting in the middle of four fires with the sun burning right over his head.
‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç in what manner, how?
‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§§ scattered, killed.
‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ç‡§õ‡§®‡§É ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§É scil. ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á (‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø).
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Ç & c, what wise person will sprinkle with water the fever (i. e. the body with the fever) called Amajvara, which must be made to sweat (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ß‡§Ç). ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø=‡§ö‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø (of Sishupala). ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ç‡§°‡§µ‡§É=‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§∞‡§É.

XXVIII.

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É connected with the Vedas.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ó‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•Ä‡§É conversations about learning.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç to be respected or adored. ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑ Name of the 6th Manu.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç gave a wrong accent (on a word), chanted a discordant tone.
‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§ ill-acquired, i. e. imperfectly acquired. ‡§Ö‡§™‡§á‡§∏‡•ç to scoff at, deride.

‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§¨‡§Ç‡§ß‡•Å a contemptuous term for a Brahmana, an unworthy Brahmana.
‡§Æ‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§ñ‡•á‡§ü‡§ï a cursed or wretched sage.
‡§µ‡•É‡§∏‡•Ä the seat of a religious student made of Kusha grass.
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø should be written ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø, though their minds be not in their usual (calm) mood, though agitated in mind.
‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç first ‡§Ö‡§®‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ú‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç of those who have not curbed their senses.
‡§Ö‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï light (here of course of knowledge) as opposed to ‡§§‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç (ignorance).
‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§Ø‡§ø‡§ï‡§§‡§æ the state of being connected or united with.
‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ (1) having round pearls (in the case of ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø), and (2) devoid of righteousness or rectitude in the case of ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø.
‡§∂‡•à‡§≤‡•Ç‡§∑ an actor, dancer.
‡§è‡§°‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§ï deaf and dumb. ‡§è‡§° deaf,
‡§®‡§ø‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•Ä‡§§‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç have punished, chastised.

XXIX.

‡§è‡§ï‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç the sole or supreme Being.
‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É not having any one else for its scope, i. e. not applicable to any one else.
‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•É‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is inwardly sought or meditated upon.
‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§∏‡•Å‡§≤‡§≠‡§É easily accessible by the application of firm devotion.
‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ the setter is to blame, the blame rest with the setter.
‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§∂‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç mastery or lordship over realms.
‡§Ü‡§∂‡§æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ã ‡§ó‡§§‡§É who has really all his desires fulfilleds (lit. who has gone to the end of his desires)?
‡§Ö‡§™‡§Ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç following a bad way or course.

‡§∏‡•Å‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§É the foremost of the most dreadful; the words are addressed to ‡§π‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§π‡§≤.
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§É in large numbers.
‡§®‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is not accessible or approachable and hence useful.
‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø means (1) capable of being vanquished or subdued (as an enemy), and (2) curable (as a disease).
‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§µ‡§¶‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ whether good or bad, (important or not).‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç stale, not fresh.
‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ç astray (figuratively also).
‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ a great officer of state, a chief minister.
‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§ó‡•ã‡§ö‡§∞‡§Ç cannot be attained by a thief (lit. one that means to take it away). ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø indescribable.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç being imparted or given away.
‡§Ö‡§Ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç hidden or secret treasure.
‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•à‡§É soil, ‡§§‡•à‡§É ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç composed,
‡§§‡§¶‡§≤‡§ò‡•Å that (well-known) and important or great.
‡§¶‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§Ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç irresistible (their spread being incapable of being prevented).
‡§ú‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á becomes or acts like water, i. e. becomes as cold as water.
‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§Ç noble or pure character.
‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç to that extent, so much,
‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§æ=‡§ó‡•ã‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡§æ yellow pigment.
‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ø arrogance, conceit.
‡§ú‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§∏‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç (thus) learning or eloquence (of a person) grows old in the body itself (wastes away without being appreciated by any one).
‡§®‡•Ä‡§ö‡•à‡§É‚Äî adv. of ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø.
‡§Ö‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ ‡§® ‡§¨‡§π‡§Ç‡§§‡§ø the spokes do not move on.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç scil ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§Ç repeatedly.
‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á dispositions undergo no change.

‡§µ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§É with his body adorned (marred) by wrinkles.
‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ú‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‚Äî ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§ú‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§®‡•á‡§™‡§•‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç goes behind the curtain in the form of the world of Yama.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§ø though having a rival or fellow-wife.
‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ó‡§æ‡§É (large) rivers that flow (directly) into the ocean, i. e. the Ganges, Godavari, Krishna & c.
‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á rises (or attains to prosperity).
‡§∞‡§ö‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§Çfact & c. brings about to an eminent degree, the cutting off of the tendency to self-willed actions.
‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§Ç & c. construe thus : ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø (‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø) ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≤‡§ò‡•Å‡§É (‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á) ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•á‡§≤‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§™‡§§‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç.
‡§≤‡§ò‡•Å‡§É (1) small, and (2) low or mean-minded.
‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç thus telling (the people ); giving to the people an illustration of.
‡§¨‡§π‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ & c. outwardly acting in a manner which is charming on account of its being entirely straightforward or upright.
‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø places for other people to hazard guesses or conjectures about. ‡§§‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§É being indifferent or neutral.
‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§Ç‡§¶‡§Ç from the roots.
‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Ø‡§ø‡§®‡§É liking to untold their gcod actions.
‡§ß‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä destroying the trees in the form of courage. This refers to the well-known fact that rivers when they swell with water destroy the trees growing close to their banks.
‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç goes with ‡§¶‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å :.
‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∂‡§Ç‡§ï‡§ß‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É possessed of unflinching courage.
‡§Ö‡§≤‡§Ç fully, completely, entirely.
‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á recognises ferms.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É perception, consciouness, knowledge.
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ & c. the eyes can see their own largeness only in a mirror.
‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É‚Äî ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§≤‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É.
‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡§ó‡•Å‡§£‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ on account of his pre-eminent quality.
‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§â‡§õ‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§µ others only breathe, that is, are only alive; so called because they do nothing useful.
‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç name of Indra’s horse (born from the ocean

along with Lakshmi, the moon, deadly poison &c.); ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§Ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø (was learnt) &c. ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç Ecil. ‡§Ö‡§∂‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø.
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ if void of contentment.
‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ born in the real sense of the word, truly born.
‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ & c. the enumeration does not proceed as far as the second or ring-finger, in other words, the person must have no match to be counted along with his name,
‡§≠‡§ú‡§§‡•á & c. wise person, if vanquished by a superior foe, either betakes himself to a foreign land, or enters into him, i. e. accommodates himself to his (foe’s) will; hence the moon entered, under the guise of reflection, the bright ocheeks of the beautiful-eyed women.
‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É having a great person for his associate or companion.
‡§∏‡§Ç‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø goes with ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ.
‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç first ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç the fear of the master.
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç the fear of those who are about him.
‡§§‡§§‡§É & c, further, the position of those in high office produces hatred among evil persons, the condition of those who have risen high finds a fall to be appropriate (one who rises is apt to fall).
‡§¶‡•à‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§ñ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§® & c. looking upwords piteously or entreatingly and concealments of his own feeling.
‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§É scil ‡§∏‡•á‡§µ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø.
‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§É(1) a mine of faults, and (2) the maker of night, ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§æ‚Äîthere is a pun on the other adjectives also.
‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§ó‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø possessed of the greatness of valour.
‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã‡§É‚Äî ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ç.
‡§Ö‡§™‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∂‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ ends in a fall.
‡§Æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡§É adj. of ‡§§‡§µ.
‡§ö‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§® & c. neither increases nor diminishes.
‡§Æ‡§π‡§ß‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç a wilderness.
‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§ö‡§Ø‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§É & c. it is the irresistible attachment to (liking for) what one is accustomed to and not hostility to (dislike for) merits.

‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•á ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ç allow your growth.
‡§∏‡§π‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•å‡§§‡§ø does not become capable of & c.
‡§Ö‡§ó‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ç‡§É there is a pun on the word. It means (1) agallochum, which, when burnt, diffuses its sweet fragrance; and (2) not great or important.
‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§É of a king (lit. of one who subsists on one-sixth part of the net revenue of the kingdom given to him by the subjects, who are to keep the remaining five-sixths for themselves.
‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§®‡§É (1) soiled with ashes, and (2) stained with (the pride of) wealth.
‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§ó‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§ó‡§Ç excessively quick in circulation.
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§π‡•ã ‡§≠‡§∞‡§É the pre-eminence of beings, sufficient for the discharge of their work, arises from their very nature and not from age.
‡§Ö‡§™‡§Ç‡§°‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§æ the absence of wisdom, inasmuch as he makes meritorious persons and things very short-lived.
‡§™‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§™‡§µ‡§Ç‡§§‡•å the sun and the moon.
‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§ö‡§Ø‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§É skilled in adding to the delight of the world.
